## Contexts in which the word **china** was used in the Senate during the 1970s

* Whom does Australia recognise as the lawful government of mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19700603_senate_27_s44/#subdebate-40-0)

* I ask the Minister representing the Minister for External Affairs: Is it not the fact that the Australian Government is adopting the international attitude that the Government on the island of Taiwan is actually the Government not only of Taiwan but also of the whole of mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-6-0)

* Our relationship with Red <span class="highlight">China</span> has been quite clear. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-6-0)

* We trade with Red <span class="highlight">China</span> in certain commodities and under certain conditions in accordance with United Nations provisions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-6-0)

* The short answer is, as I said earlier, that the Minister for External Affairs made a statement yesterday in the other place about Australia's attitude to mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> and I invite the Leader of the Opposition to read it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-6-0)

*  I ask the Minister representing the Minister for External Affairs: ls it a fact that although Great Britain recognised Communist <span class="highlight">China</span> in 1949, in the 21 years since then Communist <span class="highlight">China</span> has refused to receive an ambassador from the United Kingdom on the ground that no ambassador will be received until the United Kingdom breaks off relations with Taiwan? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-5-0)

* Does he believe that in those circumstances the Australian Government could possibly consider destroying our relations with Taiwan and establishing relations with Communist <span class="highlight">China</span>, which has treated the British diplomatic representative, the charge d'affaires, as a second class diplomatic representative and has refused under any circumstances to receive an ambassador? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-5-0)

* The views expressed by  Senator McManns  about the United Kingdom's affairs with Red <span class="highlight">China</span> are in accordance with my understanding of the position. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-5-0)

* As for relations between the United Kingdom Government and Red <span class="highlight">China</span>, that is a matter for those 2 governments. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-5-0)

* As 1 said in response to the series of questions by  Senator Murphy,  there can be no doubt that even though the United Kingdom Government and Red <span class="highlight">China</span> do have an understanding, this does not appear to have had any significant influence on the relationships between those 2 countries in the context of what  Senator McManus  said. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-5-0)

* How long is the nonsense of Australia's trading heavily with mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> and yet refusing to recognise the existence of its government to go on? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-4-0)

* ls it not a fact that many years ago the Government of Great Britain under Prime Minister  Sir Winston  Churchill recognised the existence of the Government of mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-4-0)

* How long are we to defy common sense by saying that the Government of mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> is not the Government in Peking but is actually the Government in Taiwan? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-4-0)

* Will not the Australian Government, for the sake of its citizens and to maintain any kind of dignity, follow the example of Canada and recognise the Government of mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-4-0)

* The fact of the matter is that Australia's attitude to the recognition of Communist <span class="highlight">China</span> has been clearly stated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-4-0)

* Can the Leader of the Government in the Senate ascertain from the Leader of the Opposition in the Senate whether the Australian Labor Party is in favour of selling wheat to Red <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701015_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-21-0)

* Any effects of the diplomatic recognition of <span class="highlight">China</span> by Canada on our sales of wheat to mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> at this stage can be only pure conjecture. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701016_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-3-0)

* There is no evidence to suggest that <span class="highlight">China</span> will cut down its wheat imports from Australia or turn away from Australia as a source of supply. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701016_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-3-0)

* Canada has been selling wheal to mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> in pretty large quantities only since 1961 and Australia has had wheat markets in <span class="highlight">China</span> since before that time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701016_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-3-0)

* Expressions of considerable concern have been made by people in the wheat industry and wheat growing areas throughout Australia about the likely loss to Canada of a considerable market for wheat in <span class="highlight">China</span> as a consequence of Canadia's diplomatic recognition of the Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>, coupled with problems created by the drought, the quota delivery scheme, the cost spiral and inflation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701016_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-3-0)

* Will the Minister immediately consult his colleague, the Minister for Trade and Industry, and attempt to negotiate a longterm wheat contract with the Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> which would assist in getting the wheat growing industry off the hook? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701016_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-3-0)

* At the same time will he give the marketing authority an assurance that the Australian Government will support the application of <span class="highlight">China</span> for admission to the United Nations Organisation? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1970/19701016_senate_27_s46/#subdebate-3-0)

* Having regard to the present price of wool, what would be the use of the rams in question either in Australia or in <span class="highlight">China</span>, or elsewhere? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710216_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-31-0)

* To the best of my knowledge, no wheat has been sold to <span class="highlight">China</span> in recent months. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710401_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-8-0)

* Has the Minister any comment on a recent Japanese report on the Chinese economy which stated that <span class="highlight">China</span> will buy no wheat from Australia this year? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710401_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-8-0)

* That the Senate discussthe loss of wheat sales to <span class="highlight">China</span> as a result of the attitude of the Government and the public statements of the Leader of the Country Party. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710407_senate_27_s47/#debate-1)

* I ask: Could the Leader of the Government in the Senate or the Minister representing the Minister for Foreign Affairs explain whether the Australian Government still asserts internationally that the lawful government of Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> is still the Government of the Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>, which is situated on Taiwan? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710420_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-2-0)

* Will the Government inform the Senate how long this nonsense is going to continue of Australia pretending that the lawful government of Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> is not the Government of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>, particularly as it has been recognised as such by even Conservative governments in Britain for over 20 years? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710420_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-2-0)

* I ask the Leader of the Government in the Senate: In view of the recent statement by the Prime Minister that the Government intended to liberalise trade with <span class="highlight">China</span>, and having regard also to the statement made yesterday by the Deputy Prime Minister that he now supports recognition of Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>, does the Government now support what the Australian Labour Party is trying to do in opening up new initiatives with <span class="highlight">China</span>, or does the Government intend to display initiative especially in respect of trade and diplomatic relations with that nation? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710422_senate_27_s47/#subdebate-1-0)

* Have any orders for the purchase of wheat been received this season from the Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710507_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-42-0)

* Will the Minister comment on a recent Japanese report on the economy of Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> which stated that <span class="highlight">China</span> will buy no wheat from Australia this year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710507_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-42-0)

* Is there any truth in the story that  Dr Patterson,  the Labor shadow Minister for Primary Industry, may not go to <span class="highlight">China</span> because the Australian Labor Party is now very concerned over the great opposition by the Australian Wheat Industry and the Australian Wheat Board to bringing politics into wheat sales? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710507_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-5-0)

* In 1 962 it was described as a mass organisation which, as I understand it, is a semi-official body not part pf the formal structure of the Government of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710512_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-9-0)

* It is used as a convenient vehicle for communications to non-government bodies in foreign countries with which the Government of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> wishes to communicate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710512_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-9-0)

* In view of the atmosphere of euphoria in the Press and in another quarter surrounding this matter can the Minister advise the Senate as to the identity and the authority of the body extending the recently publicised invitation to the Australian Labor Party for a delegation to visit Red <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710512_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-9-0)

* Has anything happened in the last day or so towards a normalisation of relations between Australia and the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710512_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-3-0)

* Can it be expected that an atmosphere might eventually be created in which the Government of this country could take such further assertive initiatives as would lead to a total disengagement in Vietnam and recognition of continental <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710513_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-0-0)

* He would probably incorporate the actual trading figures between Australia and mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-10-0)

* I ask: Does the Minister recall a statement on <span class="highlight">China</span> by  Mr Patrick  Shaw, the Austraiian delegate to the United Nations, on 13th November 1968? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-12-0)

* In view of the Prime Minister's statement yesterday indicating a much more favourable attitude by the Australian Government towards <span class="highlight">China</span>, can the Minister advise the Senate of the changes in <span class="highlight">China</span>'s policy which justify the [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-12-0)

* When compiling the answer to the question asked by  Senator Buttfield  relative to trade with Taiwan and continental <span class="highlight">China</span>, will the Minister list the goods upon which trade is restricted with continental <span class="highlight">China</span> in order that a proper and realistic comparison can be made? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-10-0)

* It is interesting to note that in some figures which I have it is shown that Australia's exports to the Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> in Taiwan have doubled in money value since 1968. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-5-0)

* My question is directed to the Minister representing the Minister for Trade and Industry and has particular reference to those honourable senators who claim that Taiwan-Australia interests should be submerged for those of Red <span class="highlight">China</span> and Australia in the recognition of Red <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-5-0)

* Is it a fact that the United States ambassador in Taiwan has publicly predicted that Taiwan's international trade volume may be equal to or in excess of that of mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> in 2 or 3 years' time? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-5-0)

* Is it a fact that, taking 1968 as a base year, Taiwan increased its international trade by 33 per cent last year and by 23.9 per cent in 1969 while mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> increased its trade by 6.3 per cent in 1969 and 5.8 per cent last year? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-5-0)

* Can the Minister give similar figures for the volumes and growth rates of trade between Taiwan and Australia and Red <span class="highlight">China</span> and Australia? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710514_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-5-0)

* The point is well taken that  Mr Whitlam  will search in vain for an Opposition or a Leader of it in mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710518_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-20-0)

* 
 - Mr Deputy President, I wish to take 2 minutes, if I may, to amplify a matter arising from a small misunderstanding which appears to have resulted from a question that I asked this morning in relation to the proposed visit of an Australian Labor Party delegation to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710518_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-49-0)

* POLO, MARCO (1254-1324), Venetian traveller, whose descriptions of his journeys across the world from Venice to <span class="highlight">China</span> and back, and of his experiences in the vast dominions of the Mongol emperor Kublai, make one of the greatest books of a time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710518_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-49-0)

* Its author was the first to inform the West of the extent and power of <span class="highlight">China</span>- [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19710518_senate_27_s48/#subdebate-49-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19711103_senate_27_s50/#subdebate-52-0)

* All these countries voted for the admission of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the expulsion of the Taipeh Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19711103_senate_27_s50/#subdebate-52-0)

* When one looks at the 35 nations which voted against the expulsion of the Taipeh Government and the admission of <span class="highlight">China</span>, one finds Bolivia, Brazil, Costa Rica, the Dominican Republic, El Salvador, Guatemala, Haiti - a great democracy - Honduras, Nicaragua, Paraguay, Uruguay and Venezuela. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19711103_senate_27_s50/#subdebate-52-0)

* Those countries are almost  completely dependent for their arms and the maintenance of their government upon American aid through the mis-named Alliance for Progress, lt is rather interesting to find that the threat of Communist <span class="highlight">China</span> is felt so clearly in the Dominican Republic, Haiti, Paraguay and Bolivia - where a new crowd of colonels has just taken over - but not felt in Singapore, Malaysia and Nepal. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1971/19711103_senate_27_s50/#subdebate-52-0)

* The decision of the United Nations General Assembly was that the Government in Peking was the government of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Government in Taipeh was not the government of <span class="highlight">China</span>. * Unfortunately sales to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> on which we have been dependent for some years did not eventuate. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> bought its wheat from Canada and we were left in the unfortunate position of having a large part of what we looked on as foreseeable sales taken from us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* Fortunately a market for Australian wheat became available in the Arab states which, although they were not prepared to take as much wheat as we would have exported to <span class="highlight">China</span>, bought sufficient to bring our total exports to 254 million bushels, leaving us with 125 million bushels which so far we have not been able to sell - although that does not mean that we will not be able to get rid of it before the end of the season. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* Figures which are available to me reveal that the United Kingdom was the biggest purchaser of Australian wheat, having bought wheat to the value of about $8lm; that the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> bought wheat to the value of $57m; that the United Arab Republic, which has taken some of the wheat which formerly we would have expected to sell to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>, bought wheat to the value of $56m; that Japan bought Australian wheat to the value of $40m, in round figures; and that Iraq purchased our wheat to the value of $22m. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* The other matter with which I want to deal briefly is the reference to the potential markets which are supposed to exist in Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* It would be foolish to believe that because certain changes are taking place in the international field there will naturally be a reversion to the former situation and we will sell more wheat to Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>, or even a reversion to the time when we made sales to Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> out of a few Australian crops. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* At that time the United States of America which had huge wheat surpluses- refused to sell to Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* Because America was not in the market to sell to Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> one of the most virile competitors, as far as Australian wheat sales were concerned, was removed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* This enhanced our prospects of meeting the emergency situation which forced Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> to buy wheat from us, and we cashed in. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* One of the greatest mistakes Australian producers could possibly make at this time is to think that because of a realignment of international feeling towards Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> there will naturally be a burst of buying of Australian primary products, whether it be wheat or anything else. * I suggest that anybody who doubts what I say should study the figures of the imbalance of international trade which we have had in recent years with Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> compared to the very favourable trade balance which we have enjoyed with Taiwan. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* Certainly Taiwan is a much smaller country in terms of population but in terms of international trade Taiwan trades much more, freely with the rest of the world than does Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>, which does not intend' to trade with any country if it can possibly avoid doing so. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* Obviously it is the intention of Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> to be self-supporting as far as possible and not to buy internationally any more than it is forced to. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* I sound that warning because I feel that it is much better for Australia to seek the broader markets of the world and to sell smaller quantities to a greater number of countries, than to become committed to supplying huge quantities to a particularly shaky market which could possibly exist in any primary production trading with Mainland <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720322_senate_27_s51/#subdebate-57-0)

* We had to live from 1955 until the last session of the United Nations to see the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> take its place in that body. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* I suppose that it is an irony of the universe that next to India is the greatest country in the world, in terms of population - <span class="highlight">China</span> - which adheres to a communist system of government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* As I say, in 1955 when we in the Australian Labor Party said that all nations should be admitted to the United Nations and mentioned the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> we handed to our opponents a stick with which to beat us over the head. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* Before that we divided up Ireland and Korea; <span class="highlight">China</span> divided up itself; and we divided up Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* I say that as a background to the more specific point I put in my motion - I again emphasise that it was framed 12 months ago - involving the whole question of wheat sales to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* Australia would have been in trouble with regard to wheat a long time ago if it had not been for its wheat sales to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* Mr Maisey,  who is now a member of Parliament - the honourable member for Moore - was one of the first members of the Wheat Board to suggest selling wheat to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* At that time I remember all kinds of debates raging about whether the sale was moral, whether we should sell the wheat, whether we should not sell the wheat, whether the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> was importing wheat and reselling it, or whether it was holding the imported wheat and selling its rice to other countries to flood the rice bowl in Burma, Vietnam and Thailand and so again use the trade-politico situation which, as I mentioned, the Democratic Labor Party has underlined from time to time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* Questions asked mainly by members of the Liberal Party, have been trying to point out that the situation was not as I have stated it and that the fact that Canada had recognised the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> had nothing to do with the fact that <span class="highlight">China</span> was buying wheat from Canada and not from Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* It is undoubtedly true that during the last 18 months to 2 years <span class="highlight">China</span> has been in a strong position because it has had good seasons. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* That does not alter the fact that at the same time it has had to import wheat and has moved to the Canadian prairies rather than to Australia because Canada had recognised <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* Canada came to an agreement with <span class="highlight">China</span>, getting over the difficulties of Taiwan, which made both sides reasonably happy to sign a document on this level. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1972/19720518_senate_27_s52/#subdebate-45-0)

* That leaves unanswered the question whether, if we had recognised the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> at the same time as the Canadians did, the extra imports that <span class="highlight">China</span> needed in spite of its good seasons would have been divided equally, mathematically or by some other formula between our sister dominion Canada and ourselves. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730530_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-67-0)

* It is of course a fact that both <span class="highlight">China</span> and France have nuclear weapons systems. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730530_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-67-0)

* The Australian Government has made clear its policy of consistent opposition to nuclear weapons testing in the atmosphere, by both France and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730530_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-67-0)

* If so, will it arrange for the money to be remitted to Taiwan or does it intend to seek the views of the Embassy of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> as to what action it should take in regard to this money? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730531_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-9-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730601_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-13-0)

*  It nas been suggested that Qantas Airways Ltd should operate an air service to and from <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730601_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-13-0)

* If the honourable senator were to read the documents which have been circulated he would find that the approach to the Court in respect of the Republic of France was based on a treaty called the General Act which is not applicable as between Australia and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-9-0)

* That means there is a clear legal distinction between the position of Australia and France and that of Australia and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-9-0)

* As to the possibility of atmospheric testing by <span class="highlight">China</span> I inform the Senate that Australia has made quite clear to <span class="highlight">China</span> its objections to atmospheric testing by it or any other nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-9-0)

* The honourable senator asks whether atmospheric testing or any further atmospheric testing by <span class="highlight">China</span> will affect the people of the world, including those in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-9-0)

* My question, which is directed to the Leader of the Government in the Senate, refers to the report by  Dr Cairns  on his return from Communist <span class="highlight">China</span> that he had raised the matter of tests with  Mr Chou  En-lai. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-15-0)

* Mr Chou  En-lai exhibited considerable resentment and said that <span class="highlight">China</span> would continue to conduct atomic tests in the same way as previously. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-15-0)

* As the Australian Government took the lead in mobilising international opinion against the French test's, why does not the Australian Government take a similar lead in mobilising international opinion, particularly in South East Asia and the Pacific, against the Chinese tests and drop proposals at present in train for cultural exchanges, visits of parliamentarians and trade advantages for Communist <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-15-0)

* In answer to a previous question touching on this matter I indicated that the position of Australia in relation to France is slightly different - in fact it is considerably different - from that which it has in relation to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-15-0)

* I indicated that there is such a clear difference that the General Act is not available in relation to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-15-0)

* Ultimately it is clear that the continuence of atmospheric nuclear testing by nations of the world, including France and <span class="highlight">China</span>, will affect the people of the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730605_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-15-0)

* Some will go to <span class="highlight">China</span> next week, I believe. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730606_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-37-0)

* I will not be detained here next week if I can help it while others are travelling to <span class="highlight">China</span> and Russia at the expense of the public. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730606_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-37-0)

* Everybody knows that he is going to <span class="highlight">China</span> next week. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730606_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-37-0)

* The Prime Minister is on record (Hansard 12 April) as having said that the Government believes that France and <span class="highlight">China</span> should both accede to the Limited Test Ban Treaty; and that we have protested to the Chinese Government against its failure to accede to this treaty. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730608_senate_28_s56/#subdebate-67-0)

* Dr J.  F. Cairns was feting in Australia the representatives of communist <span class="highlight">China</span> and concluding with them a trade treaty which described them as being, in the eyes of the Whitlam Government, the most favoured nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730823_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* When one recognises <span class="highlight">China</span> one does not say in the instrument of recognition that it includes Taiwan. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730823_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* One simply says that one recognises <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730823_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730823_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* These countries have a lot of problems, and they have not been helped by the manner in which we rushed in headlong to recognise <span class="highlight">China</span> when they at least had the right to expect us to consult them and talk it over. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730823_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* Can the Leader of the Government in the Senate offer any explanation as to the contention of the Prime Minister in a recent statement to the effect that French nuclear explosions in the Pacific were a monstrous proposition; also that <span class="highlight">China</span> was in danger of attack, and France was not? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730828_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-7-0)

* The Government has taken no action against <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730830_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* It is interesting to note that no member of the Government either in this House or in the other place has ever asked a question which is critical of <span class="highlight">China</span> in regard to atmospheric nuclear testing. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730830_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* The protest to <span class="highlight">China</span> was oral, so there would be no written response. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730830_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* Will the Government advise the Government of the Peoples Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> that this Government will support the unions in this country in their threat to halt all communications and trade relations with <span class="highlight">China</span> unless she immediately stops nuclear testing in the atmosphere? * Some little time ago  Dr Cairns  led a trade delegation to <span class="highlight">China</span> and he said that he protested to Chou En-lai concerning the Chinese tests, but Chou [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730830_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* En-lai become somewhat angry and replied very angrily to  Dr Cairns  and made it quite clear that <span class="highlight">China</span> was going to continue nuclear testing whether we liked it or not. * Shortly afterwards he sold his soul to <span class="highlight">China</span> for trade. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730830_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* It is noteworthy also that at one stage  Dr Cairns,  apparently in a more frank moment, said that he would support a ban on trade with <span class="highlight">China</span> if it exploded a nuclear weapon. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19730830_senate_28_s57/#subdebate-54-0)

* However, when we asked about <span class="highlight">China</span> we were told that because <span class="highlight">China</span> does not recognise the International Court of Justice there is no legal basis for taking <span class="highlight">China</span> before that Court. * I wish to make a statement relating to the visit to Japan and <span class="highlight">China</span> by the Prime Minister  (Mr Whitlam). [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* Both visits were marked by great warmth on both sides; both visits were characterised by frankness and firmness from both sides; both visits notably advanced the interests of Australia and our friendship and understanding with these 2 great neighbours, Japan and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* On the visit to Chinafrom 31 October to 4 November- I was accompanied by the Treasurer and the Minister for Northern Development  (Dr Patterson). [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* In <span class="highlight">China</span> I consider that my visit symbolised the successful ending of a generation of lost contact between Australia and the most populous nation on earth. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* Japan is our major trading partner in the world and <span class="highlight">China</span> is the only one of the world 's 5 major powers with which, until last December, we have not had any meaningful or regular official contact. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* I believe my visit to <span class="highlight">China</span> was most valuable in restoring balance to our foreign policy and in diversifying our foreign relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* I believe that the warmth of the reception I and my party received in Peking demonstrates that <span class="highlight">China</span> like Japan recognises, to a greater extent than some Australians may believe, the growing importance of Australia as a middle power, especially in the Asian and Pacific region. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* As honourable senators will know, important and valuable arrangements were made for the sale to <span class="highlight">China</span> of up to 300,000 tons of sugar per year for a three to five year period commencing in 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* It was also agreed that we should develop a planned program of cultural, scientific, and technological exchanges between Australia and <span class="highlight">China</span>, and that representative missions in these fields would be exchanged in 1974. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* Honourable senators will be pleased to know that an understanding in principle was reached between the 2 sides on travel from <span class="highlight">China</span> to Australia by relatives of Australian citizens of Chinese descent and Chinese citizens residing in Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* I believe that my visit will give new direction and increased momentum to our existing relationship with Japan and will lead to the development of a more meaningful relationship and a continuing dialogue with <span class="highlight">China</span> which, for so long- for much too long- has been a closed book to this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* It is entirely proper that the Prime Minister  (Mr Whitlam)  should table in the Parliament as soon as he can after his return a statement on the outcome of his visit to Japan and <span class="highlight">China</span> and the talks which he held there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* We welcomed when in Government those initiatives which  President  Nixon had taken, and we acknowledged also the welcome response of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the ties which subsequently were created. * We recognise particularly with <span class="highlight">China</span> that there are benefits in creating trade associations and that there is mutuality in the benefits which can be derived. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* These and other things, I believe, can be positive benefits from the visit to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* The subject of recognition was raised and this man said to  Chairman  Mao that it would help for better relations if <span class="highlight">China</span> did not interfere in his country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* Australia is going to tell the South East Asian countries that they should recognise Communist <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

* The answer to the second part of the honourable senator's question as to whether  Mr Whitlam  was going to explain Chinese policy to the rest of South East Asia is that  Mr Whitlam  was very clear that he was not going to be an advocate or an apologist for the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> but that if anybody was to discuss it with him he would make very clear what Australia's attitude was towards recognition and how we are getting on with the People 's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731107_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731128_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-33-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731204_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-11-0)

* My question refers to the reported sale of sugar to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731206_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-75-6)

* The Minister for Northern Development  (Dr Patterson)  has informed me that the Australian sugar marketing authorities were aware of his intention to discuss in Peking the question of permanent access for Australiansugar to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731206_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-75-6)

* Such discussions were a natural sequel  to  talks  Dr Patterson  had in Peking when he first visited <span class="highlight">China</span> with  Mr Whitlam  in 1 97 1 , to the signing of the Trade Agreement between Australia and the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> in July 1973, and to the efforts to sell sugar to <span class="highlight">China</span> pursuedatthe commercial level  by  the industry itself. * In dealing with the question of aid, as honourable senators know- I have said it many times- the Government's policy is to contribute to the post-war reconstruction of all countries in Indo <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731211_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-10-0)

* Having, however, learned of the honourable senator's interest in the drinking habits of his colleagues (Senate Hansard 21 November 1973, page 1954), I have ascertained that 35 bottles of champagne were consumed in flight during my trip to Japan and <span class="highlight">China</span>; 17 bottles were of Australian origin and 1 8 bottles of French. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731211_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-57-2)

* Moreover, some 360 litres of Australian champagne (80 gallons) were sent to <span class="highlight">China</span> in response to the Australian Ambassador's proposal that Australian wines be served at the Australian Government's two official functions in Peking, a reception at the Australian Embassy for 200 guests and a return banquet at the Great Hall of the people for 550 guests. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1973/19731211_senate_28_s58/#subdebate-57-2)

* whether at a time when the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics were giving actual military aid to the Forces of North Korea then engaged in hostilities against Australian troops in the field, Wilfred Burchett then had any professional relationship, remunerated or not, with either of those Governments: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740305_SENATE_28_S59/#subdebate-10-9)

* I ask the Minister representing the Acting Minister for Foreign Affairs: Is the report correct that the Chinese Government has protested about the reporting by Australian journalists based in <span class="highlight">China</span> concerning the interesting events now developing in <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-30-0)

* For that reason, despite many years of opposition by the conservative parties in Australia, one of the first actions which we took upon election was to establish diplomatic relations with the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* But it is a course with which we persevered and which we have now brought to fruition by the establishment of diplomatic relations with the People 's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* All other countries cither have taken or are in the process of taking precisely the same step which we took in recognising the People 's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> in saying that the government of <span class="highlight">China</span> was the government in Peking and not the government on an offshore island, and that if there was to be peace in our area and in the whole world, however much some may agree or disagree with the policies of the Chinese Government, we needed to have friendly relations with that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* No longer can Australia be accused of engaging in any form of aggression in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* Despite the possibilities of a settlement in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, particularly in Vietnam, the problems are by no means finished. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* What we intend to do, and what we have done, is to work within the United Nations, to work with our friends and with those countries with which we have diplomatic relations, to see that there is a secure peace in Vietnam and in Cambodia and in the whole of Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* Another major conflict, one in regard to which it seems probable that very little can be done by Australia, is the conflict which has developed between the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* However I think we have to recognise that in the case of <span class="highlight">China</span> and in the case of the Soviet Union they are countries which, with whatever favourable aspects they may present, and indeed have presented, are dictatorships and that there are disputes as to which of them should have hegemony, if not throughout the whole world, at least in part of the world between the leaders of those 2 countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* Certainly I think it has to be said that a contributing factor- I would not suggest that it is a major factor because I think there are other more important factors involved over which we never did have any influence- involved in the present intransigence of the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span> is the many years of isolation in which both countries were placed after their revolutions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* I do not think it should be any wonder that both the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span> should be extraordinarily suspicious countries, that both of them should be countries with which it is very hard for the other nations of the world to have sensible and sane dealings in view of the treatment which was meted out to both of them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* But at the same time, that action has been very mild compared with the campaigns of economic boycotts and sanctions which were carried out for almost 2 decades against the Soviet Union and against the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>, largely at the behest of the United States of America. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* I believe they are both wrong, but I think that while we are looking at the situation of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union we have to give some recognition to the historical reasons which have given rise to the difficulties which we now find in dealing with them and to see, insofar as we can, that these policies are not continued in the future because these are things to which the Australian Labor Party is opposed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* To a large extent the major difficulties between the United States of America and the Soviet Union, and perhaps to a lesser extent between the United States of America and <span class="highlight">China</span>, have been resolved as a result of some of the initiatives taken by the major powers. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* Now it seems to be generally accepted that the U.S.A. and the Soviet Union, and on the other hand the U.S.A. and <span class="highlight">China</span>, are taking all sorts of measures to prevent a conflict breaking out between those nations or any nations closely associated with them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* We have to have an agreement, a working understanding with the other super powers, whether it be <span class="highlight">China</span> or the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics.' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740306_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-42-0)

* In <span class="highlight">China</span> 's approach to relations with other countries, we find a welcome emphasis on the principles of the equality of states and respect for the rights and views of small and middle powers. * In this context, <span class="highlight">China</span>'s support for the principles of respect for the national sovereignty, independence and territorial integrity of all states can make a significant contribution to strengthening peace. * When we came into office about 15 months ago we had no relations at all with <span class="highlight">China</span>, one of the neighbours in our area, a country of 800 million people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1974/19740307_senate_28_s59/#subdebate-50-0)

* What the Government has done is to insult and to deceive the British, the Americans, the French, the Singaporeans, the Malaysians, the Cambodians and the South Vietnamese whilst picking up some more than dubious friends in <span class="highlight">China</span>, East Germany, North Korea and any other communist state that shows its head. * 1 stated that <span class="highlight">China</span>, for ideological more than economic reasons, sought to lead the Third World. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760325_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-56-0)

* I pointed out that all these programs had failed, as had similar programs in both Russia and <span class="highlight">China</span>- indicating the futility of legislation in trying to fix these problems and showing the dangers of government interference with the economy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760325_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-56-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span>, with its 800 million people, had tried to limit its population. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760325_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-56-0)

* But India was having far more problems because although its population was only 550 million- if one can use the word only' in relation to a figure like that- its area is one-third the area of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760325_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-56-0)

* He is projecting a trip to Red <span class="highlight">China</span>, as honourable senators on the Government side call it, in the near future. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760325_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-58-0)

* She has been influenced in the past by her close neighbours, <span class="highlight">China</span> and Korea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760401_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-38-0)

* In this morning's Press,  Mr Nakao,  a member of the Liberal Party in Japan and a director of the Japanese Government's Standing Committee on Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries, is reported as saying that he agrees entirely with  Mr Anthony's  comments that if Australia's resources are not made available to countries like Japan-  Mr Nakao  went on to mention Korea and <span class="highlight">China</span> as well- they will be taken from us in the years to come. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760401_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-38-0)

* We equally share, though for different reasons, concern at the developments in <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union, their impact on each of us and their impact on the region in which Australia and Japan are. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-39-0)

* We share an interest and concern in developments in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> and the Subcontinent, areas which both of us see as ones of potential instability. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-39-0)

* As I understand it the minds of the people of the dark ages were unlocked because our medieval forefathers, wishing to trade with the Spice Islands, sought a route to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-39-0)

* As a result of seeking trade they unlocked all the treasures of the East- of <span class="highlight">China</span>, Japan and the Spice Islands. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-39-0)

* I find it particularly surprising that that sort of comment should come from a member of a Party which went into an election campaign 10 years ago with an emotive slogan about the downward thrust of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-40-0)

* Some of the people who still sit in the benches across the aisle and their friends asserted that they had to stop the downward thrust of <span class="highlight">China</span> and they would not recognise <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-40-0)

* Therefore, for 3 years we sold not a ton of wheat to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760406_senate_30_s67/#subdebate-40-0)

* We must expect world wheat production again to exceed demand sometime during the next few years, particularly as <span class="highlight">China</span>, traditionally a large if inconsistent importer of our wheat, is becoming selfsufficient. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760429_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-39-0)

* Grain production in <span class="highlight">China</span> is based mainly on irrigation so it is not affected by droughts. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760429_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-39-0)

* In fact, from first hand knowledge I gained in <span class="highlight">China</span> in 1973, 1 suggest that with her increasing mechanisation, her work on breeding better varieties, her disease and insect control and, just as important, her success with population control, <span class="highlight">China</span> may very well become an exporter of wheat quite soon, in competition with Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760429_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-39-0)

* It is a world whose relations also depend however, on the actions of other major powers- <span class="highlight">China</span>, Japan and the European powers- and within particular regions also on the distribution of power between middle and small states. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* It is not in <span class="highlight">China</span>'s interests that the Soviet Union should become dominant in South East Asia, nor in Japan's interests that the Soviet Union should become dominant in the Indian Ocean. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* On the other hand, it is not, presumably, in the Soviet Union's interests that relations between <span class="highlight">China</span>, Japan and the United States should be too close. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* It means that Australia will involve itself and take sides in the dispute that exists between the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* I admit that in view of the hysteria that exists in this country from time to time there may be some political advantage for this Government in that, just as there was political advantage in 1965 in the alleged threats of <span class="highlight">China</span> coming down, with those big broad arrows from the north, to gobble us up. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* Suddenly <span class="highlight">China</span> has become respectable. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* In the eyes of the Liberal and National Country Parties, <span class="highlight">China</span> is now respectable. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* It must be seen as part of a thrust by Communist <span class="highlight">China</span> between the Indian and Pacific Oceans. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* The people of Australia were stampeded into believing that the downward thrust of <span class="highlight">China</span> was here to stay and we were to be gobbled up by the Chinese, not the Russians. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* We are told that we must show our friendliness, our common interest with <span class="highlight">China</span> even. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* It is unfortunate that there has been little time in which to document all the statements which are contained in this speech, but one thing remains paramount above everything else: There has been this dramatic change towards <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* It was a winning issue in the 1960s to put fear into people's minds that we were to be gobbled up by <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* Cannot the same question be asked of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the United States? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* Is the same question contained in the speech asked of <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* There is an entirely different tone to the attitude of the Soviet Union than there is to that of <span class="highlight">China</span> and that is quite clearly the intention. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* Senator Walters  just interjected that <span class="highlight">China</span> is not in the Indian Ocean. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> may or may not be present there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* It has one railway, the trans-Siberian railway, which for hundreds of kilometres runs very close to the Manchurian, or Chinese, border and this becomes a very vulnerable link with Russia's eastern provinces in the event of hostilities with <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760601_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-59-0)

* The report shows that our exports to mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> have actually fallen off quite substantially and that we export 5 times as much wool to Taiwan as we do to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760604_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-56-0)

* There is no significant difference in the percentages before and after we recognised the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760604_senate_30_s68/#subdebate-56-0)

* Earlier than most, he foresaw the importance of bringing <span class="highlight">China</span> into the international community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#debate-1)

* It might be argued, as  Senator Sibraa  interjected, that we should cease trade either with <span class="highlight">China</span> or Russia as super powers because of political oppression. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760818_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-66-1)

* He completely disagreed with his Prime Minister who gave this as one of his reasons for the build-up of defence in the Indian Ocean, in view of the changed relationship with Communist <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760907_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-45-3)

* It is with deep regret that I inform the Senate of the death on 9 September 1976 of Chairman Mao Tse-tung, Chairman of the Central Committee of the Communist Party of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* That the Senate records its sincere regret at the death of Chairman Mao Tse-tung, Chairman of the Central Committee of the Communist Party of <span class="highlight">China</span>, expresses to the people of <span class="highlight">China</span> profound regret and tenders its deep sympathy to his family in their bereavement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* He was the principal architect of <span class="highlight">China</span> since 1949 and one of the very few men who have had a major impact on the course of world history. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* He led the Chinese Communist Party through a long and destructive civil war and in his writings set out a new conception of what <span class="highlight">China</span> should be. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* For the first time in many decades Mao Tse-tung gave <span class="highlight">China</span> an effective administration, restored a country ravaged by civil war, and secured the basic necessities of life to <span class="highlight">China</span>'s people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* He sought for <span class="highlight">China</span> selfreliance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Under his leadership <span class="highlight">China</span> assumed a major role in world affairs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Mao Tse-tung 's conception of the desirable organisation of a society was not ours, but he achieved peace internally and respect for <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* He came to symbolise the new <span class="highlight">China</span> for his own people and for the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* In recent years, under his leadership, <span class="highlight">China</span> began to adjust her ideological objectives to the realities of world power. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* For Australians, it is of considerable significance that, as <span class="highlight">China</span>'s supreme leader, he lent his personal authority to the establishment and further development of <span class="highlight">China</span> 's relations with Australia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Chairman  Mao grew up in the old <span class="highlight">China</span> of war lords, feudalism and foreign domination of trade in its major cities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* He made a new <span class="highlight">China</span> of independence, self respect, and international status. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* When Mao was fourteen years of age he was married off, I understand against his will, in the feudal style of that era in <span class="highlight">China</span>'s history. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Sixtyfour years later it was the same Mao who invited the anti-communist President Nixon to Peking, which was a significant step in easing tension between <span class="highlight">China</span> and the United States and in bringing <span class="highlight">China</span> into the realm of international relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> has lost its helmsman with the death of  Chairman  Mao, but his legacy of a unified nation firmly advancing the welfare of the world 's most populous nation and its emergence to its rightful place in international affairs remains with us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* The Opposition regrets his death and expresses its sympathy to the people of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* I had the privilege of conveying this decision to the Ambassador of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> this morning. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* This meeting of the Administrative Committee of the Victorian Branch of the Australian Labor Party places on record a motion of condolence to the Government and the people of <span class="highlight">China</span> on the death of  Chairman  Mao, and requests  Senator Bill  Brown ... as former  Chairman  of the Party, to sign the book of condolences on behalf of the membership of this Branch, and that a copy of this resolution be sent to the Ambassador of the People 's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* He became part of the nationalist movement of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* In his early youth, because of the very strong feeling that existed in mainland <span class="highlight">China</span> about the intervention in the internal affairs of that country by many of the Western powers he became an official of the Kuomintang, which was the revolutionary movement. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* In the period from 1934 to 1936 Mao Tse-tung led a small group of men and women from one end of <span class="highlight">China</span> to the other, and 15 years later- on 1 October 1949- he proclaimed the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Whilst nobody necessarily is expected to agree with his philosophy or to understand it, it must be said that he succeeded in unifying <span class="highlight">China</span>, which had not for many centuries been unified. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> is the most heavily populated country on the earth and it was a feudal country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Of course, we in Western civilisation cannot understand much of what has happened but I think it has to be said that in his efforts to improve the living standards of the people of <span class="highlight">China</span> he largely succeeded. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* I was one of those who made an early pilgrimage to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* One could not fail to be impressed with the progress that was being made even 3 short years after the People's Liberation Army had succeeded in taking over Peking and the whole of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760914_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-0-0)

* Certainly if India were compared with <span class="highlight">China</span> or the Soviet Union or, for that matter, with its neighbour Pakistan or with the Philippines or Spain or most of the countries in Latin America, India indeed is a very democratic country and it probably still ranks amongst the most democratic countries in the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761005_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-52-0)

* I believe that this claim can be refuted by the fact that in the past in India when there were wars on two occasions with Pakistan and on another occasion with <span class="highlight">China</span>, the Indian Government never found it necessary to impose any emergency. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761005_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-52-0)

* I refer to a recent report of a nuclear test conducted by the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> and a further report of heavy radioactivity fall-out in the United States following the reported test. * There was a specific instance of the Secretary-General of the Australian Medical Association writing to the Minister for Foreign Affairs on 16 July of this year seeking advice on whether visas would be issued to people from Taiwan wishing to take part as representatives of the <span class="highlight">China</span> Medical Association in a congress of the Confederation of Medical Associations in Asia and Oceania to be held in Sydney in 1 977. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761202_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-38-0)

* In replying to  Dr Repin  the Minister,  Mr Peacock,  briefly outlined the conditions governing the entry to Australia of people from Taiwan and suggested that, as  Dr Repin  had indicated it would only be possible for participants from Taiwan to attend as representatives of the <span class="highlight">China</span> Medical Association, it seemed clear that they could not meet the conditions of entry for residents of Taiwan and therefore would not be able to obtain visas to attend the congress. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761202_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-38-0)

* In the event it appears that the AMA was unable to make arrangements for the congress which would enable people from Taiwan to take part except as representatives of the <span class="highlight">China</span> Medical Association and accordingly felt obliged to cancel plans for holding the congress in Australia. * Japan (Tokyo, Kyoto), <span class="highlight">China</span> (Peking, Tai Yuan, Urumchi, Canton) and Hong Kong: 14-29 June 1976 [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19761206_senate_30_s70/#subdebate-51-0)
