* The fact that some other countries recognise the ' Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>' in no way calls into question the effectiveness of Australia's safeguards policy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781025_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-39-4)

* Project Pyramider was described during the Boyce trial in Los Angeles in 1 977 as consisting of a number of satellites, controlled through Pine Gap, which would enable CIA agents in the field, including those in the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span>, to communicate directly with CIA headquarters in Langley, Virginia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781026_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-50-0)

* It is prompted by the recent statement by the Deputy Prime Minister to the effect that Australia can look forward to a glowing future if it enters into co-operation with the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* Does the Minister recollect that only a few years ago members of the present Government parties accused the Australian Labor Party of subversive intent when it advocated the establishment of diplomatic relations with the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> and that indeed those parties when in government - [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* Is it not also a fact that the present Government parties, when previously in government, conscripted Australians to fight in Vietnam, one of the reasons claimed for so doing being that the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> presented a threat to Australia and that Australians needed to fight in Vietnam to halt the downward thrust of menacing Chinese communism? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* Can the Minister explain to the Senate when the nature of <span class="highlight">China</span> so changed as to bring about this remarkable reversal in form by the members of the present Government parties? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* What was it that happened in <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* If the Minister is unable to do this, will he admit that the Government was wrong when it conscripted young Australians a few years ago and when it attacked the Australian Labor Party merely for wishing to have diplomatic relations with <span class="highlight">China</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* Anyone who has any understanding of what has happened with regard to the emergence of <span class="highlight">China</span> as a nation knows that for decades post-war <span class="highlight">China</span> pursued an inward-looking policy- in fact, one that did not seek to reach outwards to establish links with the outside world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* It was not Australia alone which did not have diplomatic relations with <span class="highlight">China</span> in those years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* My Government welcomes the fact that it has been able to establish good and overt working relations with a significant nation such as <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* I do not think that  Senator Wheeldon  really is serious in raising the question of IndoChina because it would do no good for his advocacy if he were to look today at the pitiful state of what is happening to the people in the IndoChina area and the absolute bloodbath of very recent years- for example, the literal bloodbath in places such as Cambodia and Laos. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* 
 -If Senator Wheeldon looks at tomorrow's  Hansard  he will find that I have indeed answered that, but I simply repeat that for several decades post-war <span class="highlight">China</span> itself pursued inward looking policies and not international policies at all. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* As a result of its inward looking policies a significant number of countries did not have diplomatic relations with <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* Along with the change of <span class="highlight">China</span>'s policies and a widening of her international links Australia in common with other countries was happy to make the diplomatic links with <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-16-0)

* When the development of nuclear weapons rendered this strategy no longer credible our strategy shifted to the possibility of a limited non-nuclear war with <span class="highlight">China</span> as part of the South East Asia Treaty Organisation alliance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781108_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-36-0)

* I direct my question to the Minister representing the Minister for Foreign Affairs and refer to continuing reports from <span class="highlight">China</span> of a growing wall poster campaign allegedly aimed against Chairman Hua Kuo-feng and supporting Vice Premier Teng Hsiao-ping. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781123_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-9-0)

* They ignored the split that had occurred between Russia and the United States, the split which occurred at that time between Russia and <span class="highlight">China</span> and the split between Russia and Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781123_senate_31_s79/#debate-62)

* Now there are splits between Russia and the United States, Russia and <span class="highlight">China</span> and Russia and Viet Nam and these do not appear to be any immediate threat to our peace. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781123_senate_31_s79/#debate-62)

* I promised to get some information to respond to a question asked by  Senator Sim  about internal political developments in <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781124_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-34-0)

* It would be premature to suggest, however, that the wall poster campaign represents a major power struggle between <span class="highlight">China</span>'s most senior leaders. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1978/19781124_senate_31_s79/#subdebate-34-0)

* The United States and <span class="highlight">China</span> have established full diplomatic relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* However, events in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, Iran, Afghanistan, and many parts of Africa demonstrate the volatility of the present international situation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* The Government has for some time identified the position in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> as deteriorating and potentially dangerous. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Prior to the fighting between Vietnam and <span class="highlight">China</span> we made known our concern to a number of governments about the dangers inherent in the situation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* In the discussions between the Prime Minister  (Mr Malcolm Fraser)  and  President  Carter in January and Prime Minister Desai later that month, they spoke about the situation in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> and about the need to exercise an influence in reducing the tensions there. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Although <span class="highlight">China</span> has indicated that it will act with prudence, there must be no underestimation of the serious danger posed to our region and the world by the present conflict between <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Australia has a vital interest in <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam swiftly and peacefully settling their differences. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* We call on Vietnam to withdraw its forces from Kampuchea, and on <span class="highlight">China</span> to withdraw its forces from Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* No-one can be certain of the course that the conflict in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> will take. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Australians are penetrating the new and important markets emerging in <span class="highlight">China</span>, South East Asia and the Middle East. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Since the end of last year events in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> have escalated rapidly and there is no sign of any immediate relief. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* On Monday last I called for a proper statement to the Parliament on the position in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* The present situation in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> is a striking example. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* In the current situation between the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span>, both countries have spoken about punishing another nation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* A month ago <span class="highlight">China</span> said it would punish Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Press reports today indicate that Russia intends to punish <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* On this occasion he is apparently on the side of <span class="highlight">China</span> and is opposed to the Soviet Union. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* He fails to appreciate how foolish it was to vilify another nation the way he did to <span class="highlight">China</span> at that time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* On 6 May 1965 he said that <span class="highlight">China</span> has not learned that the West is prepared to use force to protect its vital interests and if she wins in South Vietnam she will never accept the possibility of some kind of co-existence between her Communist regime and the West. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* Inflammatory and abusive remarks of this nature were typical of the insults that were directed against <span class="highlight">China</span> at that time not only by the present Australian Prime Minister but also by many of his colleagues. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-42-0)

* It goes right back to the first intergration of <span class="highlight">China</span> by Shih Huang Ti, the first emperor, who was a very efficient person with a very efficient bureaucracy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-53-0)

* To our knowledge <span class="highlight">China</span> was the first place in the world which identified standards of widths of roads, wheel tracks, measurements and things of that sort. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-53-0)

* That emperor was so feared and the effect of his death was so feared that when he died away from the enormous capital he had built his body was concealed for weeks by his troops in a load of rotting fish because they were afraid of the consequences to <span class="highlight">China</span> when his death was discovered. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-53-0)

* It is pretty plain that we are not going to do very well just pursuing the old paths, especially in competition with the very energetic Asian industrial revolution that is going on in such places as South Korea, Taiwan and, of course, <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-53-0)

* In <span class="highlight">China</span> I think there will be a vast industry much faster than people realise. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790222_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-53-0)

* After three and a half years of comparative quiet, South East Asia is again the scene of armed conflict- first with the Vietnamese invasion of Kampuchea, then with conflict between <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The conflicts reflect and were created by the hostility and rivalry existing among four states: the Soviet Union, <span class="highlight">China</span>, Vietnam and Kampuchea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* In our region the conflict in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> is the greatest cause of concern and I now turn to look in more detail at this and the Government's reaction to it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The basic situation which now exists in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> is a matter of great concern and disappointment to the Government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The situation began to deteriorate last year with increasing hostilities between Kampuchea and Vietnam, a worsening relationship between <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam and the signing of a treaty of friendship and co-operation, which included a military assistance clause, between the Soviet Union and Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Vietnamese attack on Kampuchea was an attack by a client of the Soviet Union on a client of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Whatever its motivation the attack bore directly on the rivalry and competition between the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span> for long term influence in the region and, more generally, on the whole Sino-Soviet dispute. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span>'s subsequent incursion into Vietnam can only be understood as a reaction to Vietnam's treaty with the Soviet Union, its invasion of Kampuchea and the installation there of a pro- Vietnamese government. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span>'s motives in striking across the border do not relate only to a border dispute but are aimed at Vietnam's political influence in Kampuchea, which is beyond <span class="highlight">China</span>'s immediate reach. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The issue between <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam therefore is not likely to be resolved with any element of permanence by a settlement on the VietnamChina border which leaves the situation in Kampuchea unchanged. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* We have called on Vietnam to withdraw its forces from Kampuchea, on <span class="highlight">China</span> to withdraw its forces from Vietnam and on the Soviet Union to exercise restraint to prevent the last turn of the screw, which could be disastrous not merely for the region but for the peace of the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Opposition has accused the Government of a pro-<span class="highlight">China</span> bias. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* To the extent that <span class="highlight">China</span> if left alone and unprovoked, would prefer peace and stability at this stage of its development in order to concentrate on internal modernisation, and only to that extent, there is a convergence between its present interest and ours. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* He emphasised that there should be immediate cease-fires in the conflicts, that Vietnam must withdraw its forces from Kampuchea and <span class="highlight">China</span> must withdraw its forces from Vietnam, and that there should be concerted efforts leading to lasting settlements, possibly using the good offices of the Secretary-General. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Some of the changes which have taken place at that level- the establishment of full diplomatic relations between the United States and <span class="highlight">China</span>, the expansion of Japan's relations with <span class="highlight">China</span>- are in themselves desirable; but what significance they will ultimately have will depend on how they fit into a picture which is not yet complete. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* It is for these reasons that we made a real effort to prevent the situation in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> from developing. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I believe that all who have followed the events there to some extent have kept their fingers crossed that the disputes, especially that between <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam, would not involve other nations and particularly the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* He does say in more places than one in the course of the speech that the Government has wished to play a constructive role in this area of dispute and yet the conflict which has really brought the immediate concern on us, namely, the Chinese attack on Vietnam, following the Vietnamese attack on Kampuchea, involves us with a couple of nations with which this Government has had much involvement over the past 10 years, and indeed in the case of <span class="highlight">China</span> going back a lot further. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* As I indicated in a speech last week, we are dealing with a government which years ago made a speciality of heaping abuse and vilification upon <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Last week I quoted some of the things which the present Prime Minister said in the middle 1960s- provocative, inflammatory remarks about <span class="highlight">China</span> which obviously could only enable that country to believe that its enemies were not only to the north and west of it but also could be very far to the south. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> has now taken the view, for reasons best understood by itself, that it wishes to take a much different and more conciliatory approach towards the United States. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Those who took the trouble to read the interview with the Chinese Vice Premier, Deng Xiaoping, in  Time  magazine only two or three weeks ago would not be left with any illusions as to the reason for <span class="highlight">China</span>'s new approach to the United States of America. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Opposition has not isolated <span class="highlight">China</span> in the world community and our record, for at least two decades, is one of ensuring that <span class="highlight">China</span> was not the odd man out. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* In 1972, before we came to Government, we took the initiative, as a party, to send a deputation to <span class="highlight">China</span> in order to try and establish a relationship between the Australian Labor Party and the Chinese authorities, one not based on hostility. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* So we do not need to apologise for or explain the fact that we have never attempted to pursue the line, or to support those who advocated the line, that <span class="highlight">China</span> should in some way be isolated from the world community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* It is quite apparent now that the present Government also does not want to see <span class="highlight">China</span> isolated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* If the Government feels that is the position, I would suggest that it not repeat the mistakes that it made in the 1950s and 1960s by forcing, or helping to force, <span class="highlight">China</span> into a state of isolation. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* He was reported in the media a fortnight ago, after a Press conference in Singapore, as saying that he was concerned with a pro-<span class="highlight">China</span> tilt developing in the Australian Government's attitude. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* He went on to say how important it is that the Government maintain a balance in its relationship between the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I reject the contention by the Minister that our criticism of a pro-<span class="highlight">China</span> attitude is an invalid one. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The whole world seems to be a tinder-box of conflicts at the moment, with the acute troubles in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, the sudden events in the Middle East and the events in Africa. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* For example, having been to the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>, I know that the Chinese are concerned about the encirclement of their country by the Russians. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Because of the conflict in Vietnam and the antagonisms between the two different communist forces in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, the Russians moved in to support one side; so the Chinese moved in to support the other side in order to prevent encirclement of their country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* This has created a dangerous situation, with a confrontation now between Russia and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Concerning Russia's intervention in Africa, Russia has not caused any of the problems in Africa, neither has <span class="highlight">China</span>, nor Britain, although all these nations have exploited the problems which already exist when it has suited their purpose. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The problems of the people of Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, Africa and even the Middle East are being aided and abetted by the foreign ambitions of the bigger powers. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* First of all there is South-East Asia where we are seeing a conflict between allegedly Marxist states- the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics; the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>; Socialist Vietnam and Democratic Kampuchea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Soviet Union, which is certainly one of the two most powerful countries in the world, and <span class="highlight">China</span>, which is at the very least one of the half dozen most powerful countries of the world, are on the very edge of armed conflict with states with which they were allied. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* In the case of <span class="highlight">China</span> it is the so-called Democratic Kampuchea and in the case of the Soviet Union it is Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* First of all let us look at the situation in South East Asia and specifically Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* After the eviction of the Japanese from Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> in 1945, when the British troops moved in, the French were brought back but clearly they were not wanted by the local inhabitants and were evicted after the battle of Dien Bien Phu in 1954. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Thousands upon thousands of people from our own country and the United States as well as from Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> died trying to preserve regimes which obviously could not last, whatever the morality of it may have been, and were bound to be destroyed. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Warring factions such as the supporters of Pol Pot, the supporters of Pham Van Dong and the supporters of the twice resuscitated First  Deputy  Premier of <span class="highlight">China</span> are brawling, fighting, murdering and bombing in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* There is scant, if any, respect for human rights in the Soviet Union, or in <span class="highlight">China</span>, or in Vietnam or in the previous and, I should imagine, present regimes in Cambodia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* We often hear romantic stories about how wonderful it is in <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I was fortunate last year to visit Japan, <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Phillippines. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Those visits were very interesting, particularly the visit to <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I now turn to the problems which exist in <span class="highlight">China</span>, Russia and Kampuchea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* When I visited <span class="highlight">China</span> I spoke to many Chinese officials. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span>'s border with Russia extends for thousands of kilometres. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I am not protecting <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I wonder whether <span class="highlight">China</span>'s invasion of Vietnam would have taken place if the Soviets had not made a treaty with the people of Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The danger is that the fighting could escalate into a war in which <span class="highlight">China</span> poured such manpower and resources into Vietnam that the Vietnamese would at last bring forward- I do not believe that they have done so yet- their crack troops to fight the Chinese. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Before the suspension of the sitting for dinner I was discussing the fact that <span class="highlight">China</span> and Vietnam are locked in battle. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I said that the time could come when <span class="highlight">China</span> would find it most difficult to extricate itself from the position in which it has now placed itself. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> has endeavoured to woo Hungary away from the Soviet bloc. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The main effect, of course, is that it is a world contest between Russia and <span class="highlight">China</span> as to which country will be the supreme being within the communist world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Although the statement of the Minister for Foreign Affairs  (Mr Peacock)  on important events throughout the world concentrated essentially on the recent developments in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, he did not review closely enough some of the mistakes that this Government has made with regard to this conflict, nor did he look sufficiently at the ramifications for the South East Asian region overall. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Sino- Vietnam conflict has made the whole of the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> and South East Asia region far less stable. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Unless there is a rapid conclusion, escalation of the conflict could well eventuate in a Soviet military strike against <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Some commentators still have not ruled out the possibility of a fullscale conventional war between <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I think that it has acted quite moderately up to the moment but I have no doubt that there are some people in the Soviet armed forces who would like to encourage a pre-emptive strike against <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I think it is also fortunate from this point of view that it is not in the interests of Vietnam to encourage a Soviet military strike against <span class="highlight">China</span> since the Chinese would then be forced to take rapid strike action against Vietnam in order to neutralise their southern flank. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I remember reading Harrison Salisbury's book in 1969 on the inevitability of a war between <span class="highlight">China</span> and Russia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* My essential criticism of the Australian Government's current approach to Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> is that we have allowed ourselves to be seen as taking a pro-Chinese stance. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Prime Minister,  Mr Fraser,  was muted in his criticism yesterday of <span class="highlight">China</span>'s attack on Vietnam, claiming that it was a direct result of Vietnam's earlier invasion of Kampuchea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Of course the same Malcolm Fraser was such a staunch critic of Gough Whitlam 's <span class="highlight">China</span> policy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Leader of the Opposition,  Mr Whitlam,  has ignored <span class="highlight">China</span>'s support for revolutionary warfare, he has ignored the fact <span class="highlight">China</span> is building strategic military roads in Asia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Whilst it is fairly obvious that the Chinese are a greater potential source of trade for Australia and that it may be of benefit to Australia to share <span class="highlight">China</span>'s attitute in regard to the demilitarisation of the Indian Ocean and a reduction of super power activity in Asia it does not justify, either on moral grounds or strategic grounds, Australia's unqualified support for <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* Frankly, that is the very real problem the world faces in the difficulty in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* However, Australia's application of its principles in the last few weeks has been to make clear in the various councils of the world its position as to the withdrawal of forces in the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> war from Vietnam as well as from Kampuchea. * However, some Opposition senators take the simplistic view that because there is a capacity for Australia to say that we require peace and stability in South East Asia, and because that view happens to coincide with the views of <span class="highlight">China</span> but apparently does not coincide with the views of Vietnam, we are somehow showing bias towards <span class="highlight">China</span>. * A very well-timed and organised force could cut that region off from the rest of <span class="highlight">China</span> and so make a quite considerable impact on <span class="highlight">China</span>'s capacity to fight a war. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* I find that the statement made by the Minister for Foreign Affairs as clearly as possible calls.upon both Vietnam and <span class="highlight">China</span> in their present conflict to withdraw their forces from the countries which they are presently occupying and to return to the establishment of peace and stability. * I am not prepared to stand here and defend <span class="highlight">China</span>'s invasion of Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

* The Vietnamese attack on Kampuchea was an attack by a client of the Soviet Union on a client of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790227_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-48-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The honourable senator has been to <span class="highlight">China</span> and he confirmed the views that I have had expressed to me by travellers to that country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Mr John  Siddons, a most distinguished Australian and the National  President  of my party, recently visited <span class="highlight">China</span> with a group of people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* He was fortunate in having as his travelling companion  Mr Ross  Tyrell, another most distinguished Australian who I think is regarded internationally as in the third top group of <span class="highlight">China</span> experts in the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* He did not say, nor do any experts say, that there is any evidence that Russia will invade <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The point is that every Chinese person sincerely believes that Russia will attack <span class="highlight">China</span> and will attack from that country's soft underbelly. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* History has shown that the invasion of <span class="highlight">China</span> from the north, the north-west and the west is difficult because of the problems presented by Mongolia and the Himalayas and with respect to logistical support. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* But invasion is a possibility with the help of friendly allies through <span class="highlight">China</span>'s underbelly- that is, up through Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Let us not forget another philosophy that has been in <span class="highlight">China</span> for many years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* One reads in Chinese literature and hears from Chinese diplomats- and this is in line with the Maoist theory- that even in the event of a nuclear war <span class="highlight">China</span> would kill 200 million of the 230 million Russians and Russia would kill 200 million Chinese but <span class="highlight">China</span> would still have 800 million people left. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I suggest that we should not play to Russia's paranoid fears- and that nation has the same fears of paranoia as does <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* If we want to have good relations with <span class="highlight">China</span>, by all means let us go out to have them. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* But let us not chase good relations with <span class="highlight">China</span> at the expense of unnecessarily offending the other great paranoid power in the world, namely, the Soviets. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I remind the Prime Minister, the Minister for Defence  (Mr Killen)  and the Minister for Foreign Affairs that if in an attempt to ingratiate themselves with <span class="highlight">China</span> they offend or play to the paranoia or the fear that is in the Russian mind they will do a great disservice to this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* For the next 25 years at least the West set about the isolation of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> in exactly the same way as the West had treated the emergence of the state known as the USSR. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* So the conditions of fear were created, and <span class="highlight">China</span> was driven into a thinking which I think is part of the underlying cause of the problem we are dealing with today. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* We all remember, of course, the statements made by the members of this Government, and the Prime Minister in particular, about <span class="highlight">China</span> and about the war in Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* We were told that it was to be the hordes of <span class="highlight">China</span> who would come down through the IndoChina peninsula and invade this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I have yet to hear a member of the conservative parties in this country acknowledge the grievous mistake that they made, that in fact they are the ones who can be termed to be the guilty ones in respect of the conflict that is taking place in the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> peninsula today. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I do not want to touch on what  Senator Chipp  said because I agree with him, as you do,  Mr Deputy President,  about the tragic events in Timor; but I want to deal with the problems in the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> peninsula as we see them at this point. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* That ignores the issues that I have canvassed and the historical developments in the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> peninsula which go back into history. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* We call on Vietnam to withdraw its forces from Kampuchea and on <span class="highlight">China</span> to withdraw its forces from Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The wars which have engulfed the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> States over the past thirty years have brought untold human suffering and misery. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* They mean precisely nothing and, of course, the document makes no reference to our areas of responsibility, whether we in fact contributed or the Western powers contributed to the dilemma, the problems and the disaster that now face the people in the Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> peninsula. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The conflicts reflect and were created by the hostility and rivalry existing among four states: the Soviet Union, <span class="highlight">China</span>, Vietnam and Kampuchea. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Whilst there are certain differences in emphasis between the major communist powers, <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union, they are not the underlying causes of the present conflict. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* As I have said, we refused to recognise <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* We refused to understand <span class="highlight">China</span>, but all of a sudden, in pursuance of this anti-Sovietism, to which  Senator Chipp  referred, we seem to be adopting a pro-<span class="highlight">China</span>, anti-Soviet position as if that were the only issue that ought to be considered in respect of the problem concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* In recent months the Iraqi Government has been spending a lot of its time beheading its pro-Soviet leaders but despite that, despite <span class="highlight">China</span>, despite Rumania, despite Yugoslavia, we now suppose that Iran, Ethiopia, Angola and Afghanistan are permanent creatures of Soviet policy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* We contributed, as part of the West, to the isolation of <span class="highlight">China</span> and we contributed to the problems in Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* There was an opportunity to create an Asian Yugoslavia, an independent country, following its own social path of development, but making its decisions of selfdetermination and not being pan of the <span class="highlight">China</span> bloc, which the Liberal-National Country Parties said was the cause of the war in Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> agreed to contribute $300m, but unfortunately, as the events show, that was cancelled at the end of last year. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* A few months later, by the spring of 1977, it had become evident that Hanoi was bent on improving relations with <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* We propose that the independence and sovereignty of Kampuchea be guaranteed by international agreement and that the Kampuchean people be left to resolve their internal problems free of interference from Vietnam, <span class="highlight">China</span> or any other outside forces. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Now we have the USSR against <span class="highlight">China</span>; <span class="highlight">China</span> against Vietnam; Yugoslavian troops on the Bulgarian border; African countries with Soviet-type dictatorships fighting each other; and Ethopia fighting Somalia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* As somebody said- I think he put it quite nicely- from Algeria to Tanzania, from <span class="highlight">China</span> to Canada, the national inspiration and the need to embody the culture in a national estate and a national society are still with us. * Of course, <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union came into this. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* But to me the lesson was this: As far as the Western powers- we could call them that or a loose alliance of the ANZUS powers- are concerned, if we look at it strictly on percentage lines, we are no better off than we would have been if we had not worried about the futile war in Vietnam because by now the ideological rivalries between <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union concerning the land mass of Asia, in particular South Vietnam, would have been apparent. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The major issue- the present conflict between Vietnam and <span class="highlight">China</span>- has had a pretty fair hammering. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* To me the question is not whether the United States, the Soviet Union or <span class="highlight">China</span> are involved. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* As a  National Times  article March 6-11,1978, stated: Australia is to play a much more significant role in the strategic weapons plan of the United States, the Soviet Union and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* It seemed to me to be the height of hypocrisy for Government members to show now so much respect for a delegation from <span class="highlight">China</span> when some six years ago they were the greatest spokesmen against <span class="highlight">China</span> and made statements about the downward thrust of communism, with the force behind that downward thrust being <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* If, in the past, we criticised the United States for its position in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, then surely we should be criticising today the position that <span class="highlight">China</span> takes against Vietnam. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Those criticisms which I levelled against the United States in adjournment debates early in the morning, I level now against <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Australia will be one of those expendable targets because it has upon its soil at the present time a number of United States bases which are aimed at monitoring the strength of the USSR and of the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* This was an invasion, and Vietnam deserved a lesson which <span class="highlight">China</span> proceeded to teach it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I was in Hanoi seven months ago and when I returned I said that the situation in Vietnam was serious; that there were 15 Chinese divisions massed on the northern border in order to reduce the pressure on Cambodia; that Vietnamese divisions were going north; and that <span class="highlight">China</span> had engaged in a psychological campaign against the Vietnamese. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* It did to the Vietnamese people what it accused the Soviet Union of doing to itself, which is at the basis of the conflict between the People's Republic of <span class="highlight">China</span> and the Soviet Union. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I refer to the sudden withdrawal of aid by the Soviet Union from <span class="highlight">China</span> at a crucial time in <span class="highlight">China</span>'s development. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> did to Vietnam exactly what it accused the Soviet Union of doing to itself. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Many of this merchant class in the South were Chinese who had fled from the revolution in <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The claim by <span class="highlight">China</span> that Chinese nationals were being persecuted arose from this incident and it seems to me peculiar that <span class="highlight">China</span> should accuse Vietnam of something which it did itself after the revolution. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* It is surprising to me that <span class="highlight">China</span> should come to the defence of Chinese merchants in Ho Chi Minh City who were refugees from the regime in <span class="highlight">China</span> and who subsequently, when they left Vietnam, went not back to <span class="highlight">China</span> but to France and, as most of them did, to Taiwan. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* When the ships that came from <span class="highlight">China</span> to pick up refugees anchored outside Haiphong, the only condition that the Vietnamese people put on the refugees leaving was that it should be done in the normal way; that lists should be given to the Vietnamese authorities of people wishing to go; that the Chinese ships could take only three days for the whole of the operation; and that they should enter only two pons, Haiphong and Ho Chi Minh City. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* My belief is that <span class="highlight">China</span> manufactured a case against Vietnam in order to invade Vietnam and to teach it a lesson because it felt that Vietnam was very much a pan of the Soviet system and part of the Soviet sphere of influence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Because it was not allowed by <span class="highlight">China</span> to do this, <span class="highlight">China</span> subsequently was able to use this to justify its invasion. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* The Australian Government has evidenced by its reception of the Chinese delegation here tonight and the subservience it is now showing to <span class="highlight">China</span> that it is taking part in a dangerous exercise. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I believe that the United States also is engaged in the same dangerous exercise of encouraging <span class="highlight">China</span> and is taking sides against the Soviet Union. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* I believe it was quite wrong of the Australian Government to have received the delegation from <span class="highlight">China</span> at a time when <span class="highlight">China</span> was engaged in an act of aggression, irrespective of how the Australian Government may have viewed the Vietnamese incursion into Cambodia. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> is a major nation, one of the four world powers. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* For some reason we now seem to think it is to our advantage that <span class="highlight">China</span> is strongly opposed to the Soviet Union, as a result of which we believe we may be able to engage in some further trade negotiations with <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* Because we have this belief we take a very short-sighted position and support <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

* This shock leads to a disturbed state of mind when contemplating a conflict between the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics and <span class="highlight">China</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-46-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-48-0)

* It would appear that the Government is making excuses for <span class="highlight">China</span> and has decided that it is far easier to withdraw aid than to abandon trade. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790306_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-48-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790308_SENATE_31_S80/#subdebate-39-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790321_senate_31_s80/#subdebate-37-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790328_senate_31_s80/#debate-37)

* As the House is aware, the Government has commissioned an intelligence assessment following recent unsettling events in the Middle East and in Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span> and its frontier with <span class="highlight">China</span> and elsewhere. * Finally, the third body that attracts  Mr Justice  Hope's explicit attention, at page 48 of the report in question, is the CPA(M/L), the <span class="highlight">China</span>-line communist party which recently, of course, found itself split into two rather bitterly-opposed factions, with its barely 1,000 members divided between those who pledge undying loyalty to the Gang of Four and the Cultural Revolution and those- the larger group- who support the current more pragmatically-inclined Chinese leadership. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790403_senate_31_s80/#debate-50)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790404_senate_31_s80/#debate-41)

* <span class="highlight">China</span> may be tainted because it executes its political opponents. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19790404_senate_31_s80/#debate-41)

* Is the Minister representing the Minister for National Development aware of a report in a recent producers' journal which says, inter alia, that because of the availability of oil from <span class="highlight">China</span> and Mexico, Australia need not be unduly concerned about potential shortfalls in oil supplies from Iran? * Apart from the intra-Australia problems we have heard about, in this regard we only have to look to our north, to Timor, to New Guinea, to Indo-<span class="highlight">China</span>, to <span class="highlight">China</span> itself and to Russia.
